  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_270f625d-c419-46c6-bcc0-b07ee569cfe1'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer285655372892631695">Ten thousand years ago, Morpheus condemned a woman who loved him to Hell. Now the other members of his immortal family, The Endless, have convinced the Dream King that this was an injustice. To make it right, Morpheus must return to Hell to rescue his banished love -- and Hell's ruler, the fallen angel Lucifer, has already sworn to destroy him.<br/><br/>Collects THE SANDMAN #21-28.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1740118554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1740118554" />
    <a title="Bill Kerwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83582-bill-kerwin"><img alt="Bill Kerwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442940975p2/83582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1740118554?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Kerwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Kerwin" href="/user/show/83582-bill-kerwin">Bill Kerwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401230425" href="/book/show/8462092-season-of-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83582-bill-kerwin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83582-bill-kerwin?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83582-bill-kerwin?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83582-bill-kerwin?shelf=weird-fiction">weird-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740118554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17010027090735793647"><br/>Neil Gaiman is at his best when his imagination is peopled with gods and demons—magnificent, outsize personalities, ranging from the eerily transcendent to the surprisingly human—and the tale he chooses to tell in “Season of Mists” gives him ample room to create a godly and superior fantasy.<br/><br/>The plot is simple. Lucifer abdicates the throne of Hell, sending the damned back to earth, and turns the keys over to Dream. Dream doesn’t really want the property—too vast, too hard to keep up—but a lot of </span>
  <span id="freeText17010027090735793647" style="display:none"><br />Neil Gaiman is at his best when his imagination is peopled with gods and demons—magnificent, outsize personalities, ranging from the eerily transcendent to the surprisingly human—and the tale he chooses to tell in “Season of Mists” gives him ample room to create a godly and superior fantasy.<br /><br />The plot is simple. Lucifer abdicates the throne of Hell, sending the damned back to earth, and turns the keys over to Dream. Dream doesn’t really want the property—too vast, too hard to keep up—but a lot of other beings do, including demons, angels, fairies, and (yes, of course) gods): Odin, Thor, Loki, Anubis, Bes, Bast, the Shinto storm god Susano-o-no-Mikoto, and the personifications of Order (a cardboard box carried by a genie) and Chaos (a little girl dressed like a clown). The delightful center of the tale is a grand banquet in the house of Dream, where these beings offer their bids and bribes for the prize of an empty Hell. One of these offers interests Dream greatly: a chance to rescue his lover Queen Nada from the consequences of his youthful anger.<br /><br />The central story is handled expertly, and the major digression—about dead schoolboys and masters returning to their boarding school during vacation—is very good too. <br /><br />Gaiman's inspiration for <i>Season of Mists</i> was a remark of Jesuit theologian and anthropologist Teilhard de Chardin: “You have told me, O God, to believe in hell. But you have forbidden me to think...of any man as damned.” An easily resolved paradox, Gaiman thought to himself, provided you empty Hell. The title is derived from Keat’s “Autumn”: “season of mists and mellow fruitfulness.” Although the association of “mellow fruitfulness” with Hell may seem ironic, I believe its message is straightforward. In <i>Season of Mists</i>, Dream does become more "mellow'" dying to unwelcome burdens and ancient rages, and gaining the fruits—a small portion, at least—of peace, reconciliation and love. <br /><br />Finally, I would like to share with you my favorite part of <i>Season of Mists</i>. Isn’t it funny how often a minor character may fascinate you so much he almost blots out the rest? For me, that character is Breschau of Livonia. This imaginary Eastern European noble (I know he’s imaginary, having looked him up in vain) proudly insists he remain in Hell because of the enormity of his deeds, which he relates in detail, proclaiming “I am Breschau of Livonia.” Lucifer dismisses him with these words: “But no one today remembers Breschau. No one. I doubt one living mortal in a hundred thousand could even point to where Livonia used to be, on a map. The world has forgotten you.” <br /><br />Not I, Lord Breschau, not I.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17010027090735793647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2042282892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2042282892" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042282892?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401230425" href="/book/show/8462092-season-of-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=darkness-horror-gothic">darkness-horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=comic-graphic-novel">comic-graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042282892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6363163664896986380">I find myself at a loss for words whenever I come to review a volume of this series, simply because it is just that good. What is there to talk of that will do it justice? Could I speak of the intelligent weaving of mythological figures with distinctively human personalities? No. Not enough. Could I speak of the literary allusions and most apt references to long dead poets and writers? No. Not enough. One thing I can say with absolute certainty is that <b>
  <u>Gaiman is a genius.</u>
</b><br/><br/>This is by far the b</span>
  <span id="freeText6363163664896986380" style="display:none">I find myself at a loss for words whenever I come to review a volume of this series, simply because it is just that good. What is there to talk of that will do it justice? Could I speak of the intelligent weaving of mythological figures with distinctively human personalities? No. Not enough. Could I speak of the literary allusions and most apt references to long dead poets and writers? No. Not enough. One thing I can say with absolute certainty is that <b>
  <u>Gaiman is a genius.</u>
</b><br><br>This is by far the best thing he has written. As great as some of his other writing is, <i>The Sandman</i> series is on a whole new level. The writing here tackles marvellously big concepts in such a clear and careful way. Dream, Death, Fate, Desire, Delirium, Despair and Destruction are powerful concepts that move human existence. In part, they help to define it. Gaiman represents them as a dysfunctional family, as forces, working to keep the balance within the universe. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499590109i/23247158._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Central to this series is Dream. And everybody does it, even the Devil himself. Lucifer has had enough of ruling in hell and wants to go and experience a few new things, only natural really after ruling in the fire pit for thousands of years. Dream grants his request and as such is left with the keys to hell itself as Lucifer goes on seemingly indefinite vacation. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458043189i/18435738._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499590168i/23247162._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Dream has his own responsibilities; he can’t be the new lord of hell. So he gives the keys away, though who could be suitable for such a task? All manner of beings come to claim them. Anubis, Thor and Odin, The King of Fay, some demons from hell and even a few of god’s chose angels come to observe the decision making. All appear unequal to the task; they all have their own personal motives and seek nothing but more power. They attempt to manipulate Dream; they use death threats, bribery and even resort to the use of hostages in order to sway him.<br><br>Dream, however, is revolute and understands that all power must be balanced within the universe. The central story is very strong, though what I saw here was the beginning of all the loose threads coming together. As grand as this story felt, it is clearly just a small chapter in a much larger story that is only just starting to reveal itself. This series seems to be picking up some momentum. Good things are sure to be ahead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6363163664896986380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer833095808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12843076407891776552">This is the point in the series where shit gets real. <br/><br/>For one thing, this is the first glimpse you have of how truly mythically all-encompasing this series is. You have Odin, the Lucifer, some Faeries, Demons, a Japanese storm god, Bast and Anubis, two angelic presences, and other assorted powers all hanging out, not just in the same story. But on the same page. <br/><br/>And it makes sense. You're left thinking, oh, yeah. Sure. Why wouldn't Thor be hitting on Bast? <br/><br/>Even more importantly, this is the poin</span>
  <span id="freeText12843076407891776552" style="display:none">This is the point in the series where shit gets real. <br /><br />For one thing, this is the first glimpse you have of how truly mythically all-encompasing this series is. You have Odin, the Lucifer, some Faeries, Demons, a Japanese storm god, Bast and Anubis, two angelic presences, and other assorted powers all hanging out, not just in the same story. But on the same page. <br /><br />And it makes sense. You're left thinking, oh, yeah. Sure. Why wouldn't Thor be hitting on Bast? <br /><br />Even more importantly, this is the point where, when I first read it, I thought. "Wait. What? Do you mean that all those cool little stand-alone stories *weren't* stand alone stories? Are you telling me that all these tiny stories (which I loved, and would have left me completely blissed and satisfied all by themselves) are actually all part of a bigger story?" <br /><br />My mind was blown. And it still kinda is. I'd never seen this done before, and I've never seen it done as well since. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12843076407891776552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_755949826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755949826" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755949826?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401230425" href="/book/show/8462092-season-of-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=comic-book">comic-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755949826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7898003051192006317"><b>
  <u>The story goes to Hell, in more than one sense.</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><u>Creative Team:</u><br/><br/>Writer: Neil Gaiman<br/><br/>Illustrators: Kelly Jones, Malcolm Jones III, Mike Dringenberg, Matt Wagner, Dick Giordano, George Pratt & P. Craig Russell<br/><br/>Covers: Dave McKean<br/><br/>Letterer: Todd Klein<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>FAMILY REUNIONS, HELLISH KEYS, BOARDING SCHOOLS & DIVINE PARTIES</u>
</b><br/><br/>Yet another impressive introduction to the TPB by Harlan Ellison, denoting again that <i>The Sandman</i> is something else in the middle of the genre of comic books.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Sometimes we can choose t</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7898003051192006317" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>The story goes to Hell, in more than one sense.</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><u>Creative Team:</u><br /><br />Writer: Neil Gaiman<br /><br />Illustrators: Kelly Jones, Malcolm Jones III, Mike Dringenberg, Matt Wagner, Dick Giordano, George Pratt &amp; P. Craig Russell<br /><br />Covers: Dave McKean<br /><br />Letterer: Todd Klein<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>FAMILY REUNIONS, HELLISH KEYS, BOARDING SCHOOLS &amp; DIVINE PARTIES</u>
</b><br /><br />Yet another impressive introduction to the TPB by Harlan Ellison, denoting again that <i>The Sandman</i> is something else in the middle of the genre of comic books.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Sometimes we can choose the path we follow. Sometimes our choices are made for us. And sometimes we have no choice at all.</i>
</b><br /><br />This volume has an epic beginning with a reunión of the members of the Endless, well all of them except the “prodigal Destruction” who went awol lefting behind his responsibilities.<br /><br />This family reunión of the Endless is easily the strongest section of the TPB and a real pleasure to read.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Come in. Everybody’s here... ...and I do mean everybody.</i>
</b><br /><br />The rest of the TPB and the main storyline developed in this volume has a wonderful premise but that I humbly think that it wasn’t properly exploited to its full potential.<br /><br />Morpheus, the embodiment of Dream committed an injustice long time ago. <br /><br />In the volumen <i>The Doll’s House</i> is told the tragic love story of Queen Nada, a mythical ruler of a vey ancient kingdom, and whose sad tale has been transmitted through generations when men reached maturity age. Nada fell in love with Dream, but loving an Endless member is something... complicated to say the least.<br /><br />Morpheus is going to Hell looking for Nada, since he found her there in his previous trip to the Hellish realm while he was looking for his mask to gather all his lost power during his imprisonment by magic.<br /><br />Hell is empty. Lucifer quit. Really.<br /><br />And now Morpheus is left with the Key to Hell. Literally the key to open or to close, Hell.<br /><br />This unprecedent event will provoke an unique gathering of gods and divine envoys of many origins (Norse, Japanese, Egyptian, Christian, etc...) even embodiments of primal forces.<br /><br />Everybody wants the Key to Hell and Morpheus is the one who will decide!<br /><br />At that point, I was astonished, my mind was in neuronal fireworks! <br /><br /><b>However...</b><br /><br />The developing of that hallucinative premise was, mmh... how to say it? ... Simple? Lacking of a real challenge to the main character (Morpheus)?<br /><br />There were so many possibilities, so many paths to take, a wide open field of odds, and at the end (without spoiling anything) is like... mmh... okay... while more the things change, more remain the same?<br /><br />Oh, and in the middle of that, you will find also a cool ghost story happening in a boarding school that I enjoyed a lot.<br /><br />So, while it contains incredible cool characters and a smart narrative, I found the ending, weak and unadventurous.<br /><br /><b>BUT...</b><br /><br />Certainly I will keep reading this epic run of <i>The Sandman</i>, you can bet on that!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7898003051192006317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer570482175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10591712704817529614">Re-Read, 4/4/20:<br/><br/>Oh, honestly, I shivered throughout the re-read. This is SUCH an important volume for the rest of the tale. And I really can't top my original review, either. <br/><br/>What a great twist this volume is. :)<br/><br/><br/>Original Review:<br/><br/>Now the good stuff really gets started.<br/><br/>Introducing most of the Endless, we discover intrigue with Destiny, some deep sadness in Delirium, friendship in Death, capriciousness in Desire, and maybe a bit of reasonableness in Despair. Dream is there, of course, and he's right</span>
  <span id="freeText10591712704817529614" style="display:none">Re-Read, 4/4/20:<br /><br />Oh, honestly, I shivered throughout the re-read. This is SUCH an important volume for the rest of the tale. And I really can't top my original review, either. <br /><br />What a great twist this volume is. :)<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />Now the good stuff really gets started.<br /><br />Introducing most of the Endless, we discover intrigue with Destiny, some deep sadness in Delirium, friendship in Death, capriciousness in Desire, and maybe a bit of reasonableness in Despair. Dream is there, of course, and he's rightly annoyed with his siblings.<br /><br />He is, after all, the one who had perpetrated a great crime. Who are they to taunt him?<br /><br />Ah, Nada. Such a tragic figure.<br /><br />And she's only a plot hook!<br /><br />Oh Hell... I'm not going to spoil Hell, but Dream goes back to right his great wrong.<br /><br />I was so surprised with the outcome. Delighted. Flabbergasted. The implications were enormous and made me giddy with anticipation. <br /><br />If the Eternals weren't enough to make things interesting, we also get the Aesir, Angels, Chaos, Chinese Gods, Devils, Fae, and Order knocking on Dream's door to threaten, bribe, plead. So totally delicious.<br /><br />I read American Gods before Sandman, so I was grooving to this tune and this twist in a big way. Hell, this Volume epitomizes everything I love about the Sandman Series. When it thinks big, it thinks BIG. Let's not piddle around the the little crap, shall we? Let's move Heaven and Earth.<br /><br />Woo! Woo! If only all comics could get this grandiose! (Of course, I later learned that some could get pretty close, but this is my first taste of something really good.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10591712704817529614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17281440656475649474">After a particularly unpleasant family reunion, Morpheus finds himself planning yet another journey to Hell. Considering the resounding defeat of the demon Choronzon back in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23754.Preludes___Nocturnes__The_Sandman___1_' title='Preludes & Nocturnes (The Sandman, #1) by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Preludes & Nocturnes</a>, Dream is understandably preparing for the worst. Such as moving a meet-up 99 years ahead, should he fail to make the next rendezvous.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603015606i/30253353.jpg' alt='Farewell toast' width='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>With volume 3 leaving me closer to unimpressed than actual enjoyment, I had almost resigned myself to forgetting about the series, but then I remembered that I still have </span>
  <span id="freeText17281440656475649474" style="display:none">After a particularly unpleasant family reunion, Morpheus finds himself planning yet another journey to Hell. Considering the resounding defeat of the demon Choronzon back in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23754.Preludes___Nocturnes__The_Sandman___1_" title="Preludes &amp; Nocturnes (The Sandman, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludes &amp; Nocturnes</a>, Dream is understandably preparing for the worst. Such as moving a meet-up 99 years ahead, should he fail to make the next rendezvous.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603015606i/30253353.jpg" alt="Farewell toast" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With volume 3 leaving me closer to unimpressed than actual enjoyment, I had almost resigned myself to forgetting about the series, but then I remembered that I still have eight volumes to go through. And since one of them is in hard-cover, that seemed like <em>way</em> too much money to just <del>throw out</del> give away.<br><br>To its credit, the volume came with a lot of amazing scenery from Destiny's domain, Hell and Asgard. Some intriguing (even if mainly confusing) back story from other religions, plus some hilarious political negotiations. The character design on the other hand, is still baffling me. I can accept that Elizabethan Dream and 80's-punk Dream only have hair color and skin tone in common, at least the style difference is specifically addressed. But Eve's drastic weight loss between two consecutive frames doesn't seem to serve any purpose... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603020543i/30253708.jpg" alt="Inconsistent character design" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My favorite part of this volume was by far Lucifer's explanation for Hell's raison d'être. I liked how it made things appear largely fair, yet with the occasional heart-breaking exception... which <em>totally</em> made me want to flip out. I wonder just how many curses I'd get if I tried to shove those sequences in some devout Christian's face? That being said, I think I've been binging <em>The Big Bang Theory</em> for way too long (11 seasons in a month is definitely too much)...<br><br>On a somewhat unrelated note: Death showing up for duty rocking 80's aerobic gear makes for a hilarious mix of offensive <em>and</em> awesome.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603022094i/30253768.jpg" alt="Death in 80's aerobic gear" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Score : 3.7/5 stars</strong><br><br>Not quite up to the excitement from the 1st volume, but I enjoyed the story, and some of the strange mix of horrific/sensual imagery. I feel like I should be more disturbed by that last bit. Ah well, should anyone ask: all those creepy hentai doujinshi have desensitized me. <strong>*cue shifty eyes*</strong><br><br>Suffice to say: the series still feels full of potential, and I'm looking forward to exploring more of the details hinted at in this volume.<br>============<br>Review of volume 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2958722582" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludes &amp; Nocturnes</a><br>Review of volume 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3013180156" rel="nofollow noopener">The Doll's House</a><br>Review of volume 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3013179860" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream Country</a></span>

<div id="review_2657649631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2657649631" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2657649631?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401230425" href="/book/show/8462092-season-of-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2657649631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2946133575081931625">"I think hell’s something you carry around with you. Not somewhere you go."<br/><br/>Season of Mists is the fourth volume in the Sandman graphic novel series. Lucifer has given Dream the key to Hell, however Dream has a lot of other responsibilities and so decides the key should be given to someone else - but who?<br/><br/>Oh man, this has definitely been my favourite volume so far in the series. I have been enjoying Sandman a lot, but this was the point at which I really began to understand the hype behind it. Sea</span>
  <span id="freeText2946133575081931625" style="display:none">"I think hell’s something you carry around with you. Not somewhere you go."<br /><br />Season of Mists is the fourth volume in the Sandman graphic novel series. Lucifer has given Dream the key to Hell, however Dream has a lot of other responsibilities and so decides the key should be given to someone else - but who?<br /><br />Oh man, this has definitely been my favourite volume so far in the series. I have been enjoying Sandman a lot, but this was the point at which I really began to understand the hype behind it. Season of Mists opens up with an Endless family gathering - and all are present and accounted for - Dream, Death, Desire, Delirium, Despair, Destiny and Destruction. I am obsessed with this concept, that these components that play a role in each human's experience are represented by a dysfunctional family of seven siblings. It's frigging genius how Gaiman does this, I am simply IN AWE.<br /><br />Following some taunting at the family get-together, Dream feels bad about his treatment of a former lover and decides to go to Hell to retrieve her, but upon his arrival he finds that Lucifer is driving out all the demons and damned souls and he gives Dream the key to Hell's gates. THEN the fun really starts as we get an amazing mishmash of different mythologies coming together - baring some resemblance to American Gods - to visit the Dreaming and plead their case to Dream for the key. You got Odin arriving alongside Loki and Thor... as well as Anubis, Bast and Bes.... the list goes on. So many crazy and vibrant characters, I can't compliment this aspect enough!<br /><br />Amongst all the drama happening over at the Dreaming, we also get a chapter that gives us some insight into the consequences of Hell's closure. And it's EXCELLENT.<br /><br />I'm honestly at a loss for words in terms of describing how much I loved this volume, although I feel like perhaps the reason I thoroughly enjoyed this one was because it is really the first to have a consistent story arc.<br /><br />Gaiman's imagination continues to fascinate me, he is just on another level. 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2946133575081931625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_400685086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400685086" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400685086?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-superhero-scifi-fantasy">gn-superhero-scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400685086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14742592393196315410">A 2020 reread.<br/><br/>Okay, when I first read I thought: this is obviously very good, but unlike most of the Gaiman universe, I liked the intimacy of volume 3 more than this huge, epic, operatic occasion where Morpheus decides what to do with Hell after Lucifer hands it over to him. But this time I see that this is what Gaiman does best, to alternate between a grand operatic canvas and the intimacy of the simple story. And it is a simple story, a kind of mythical allegory: With some poignancy Dream dete</span>
  <span id="freeText14742592393196315410" style="display:none">A 2020 reread.<br /><br />Okay, when I first read I thought: this is obviously very good, but unlike most of the Gaiman universe, I liked the intimacy of volume 3 more than this huge, epic, operatic occasion where Morpheus decides what to do with Hell after Lucifer hands it over to him. But this time I see that this is what Gaiman does best, to alternate between a grand operatic canvas and the intimacy of the simple story. And it is a simple story, a kind of mythical allegory: With some poignancy Dream determines (influenced by his sisters!) that the best thing he could do to right a wrong he did to an ex-lover is to Go to Hell himself and release her (yep, he did that, not okay at all). Then, when he is in Hell, many gods from various worlds vye for ownership of Hell, and he creates ingenious solutions to both dilemmas (especially, that Nada, thus released, becomes transformed into a babe, without memory). What he did--ugh, this doesn't make it right, but it's still a fine sweet ending after all the High Fantasy.<br /><br />Dream realizes, in other words, that he has made a mistake, as he has himself just been recently released from captivity. He was a colossal jerk, and almost as if human, makes restitution for his sin. <br /><br />There's another interlude that is deliciously creepy about a kid who goes to a school with ghosts from Hell. It doesn't quite fit with the rest, I think, but I liked it. This Sandman is like the Paradise Lost of comics, an epic, and this volume is as good as it gets. And sets up Mike Carey's Lucifer spin-off.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14742592393196315410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1188968671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1188968671" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1188968671?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1188968671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8928593584619871118">“So I'm back, to the velvet underground<br/>Back to the floor, that I love<br/>To a room with some lace and paper flowers<br/>Back to the gypsy that I was<br/>To the gypsy... that I was<br/>And it all comes down to you<br/>Well, you know that it does<br/>Well, lightning strikes, maybe once, maybe twice<br/>Ah, and it lights up the night” (Nicks: Welsh Witch Music)<br/><br/>When I think about Neil Gaiman’s work, it all comes back to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_' title='American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>American Gods</a>. This is the book by him that to me is the most identifiable of his canon and the work upon so much </span>
  <span id="freeText8928593584619871118" style="display:none">“So I'm back, to the velvet underground<br>Back to the floor, that I love<br>To a room with some lace and paper flowers<br>Back to the gypsy that I was<br>To the gypsy... that I was<br>And it all comes down to you<br>Well, you know that it does<br>Well, lightning strikes, maybe once, maybe twice<br>Ah, and it lights up the night” (Nicks: Welsh Witch Music)<br><br>When I think about Neil Gaiman’s work, it all comes back to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a>. This is the book by him that to me is the most identifiable of his canon and the work upon so much other writers have accessed influence. Certainly there have been trans-pantheistic works prior to the 2001 publication of AG, but I think Gaiman put it all together best.<br><br>Season of Mists, the fourth collection in the Sandman graphic novel series was published in 1992 and this must have been on Gaiman’s mind when a few years later he began his seminal work. Sandman readers once again visit Dream in his world and we also see Hell and much chaos and confusion. Odin All-father appears, as do Thor and Loki, but his illustration is very similar to how he would later appear in Gaiman’s 2001 masterpiece.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423945i/844955.jpg" width="400" height="185" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

What begins as the weirdest family reunion of all time takes a turn when Dream’s family calls him out for the very douche bag move of condemning his ex-girlfriend to eternal damnation in a fit of pique because she totally wanted to date other people. Dream decides to journey to Hell to save her soul and hijinks ensue, not the least of which involves <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view s</a></span>
  <span id="freeText9477284033750748059" style="display:none">I’ve been gradually warming to this series as it’s picked up momentum, and Vol. 4 proved to be a glorious realization of its vast potential. What begins as the weirdest family reunion of all time takes a turn when Dream’s family calls him out for the very douche bag move of condemning his ex-girlfriend to eternal damnation in a fit of pique because she totally wanted to date other people. It’s delightful good fun. <br /><br />Onward to Vol. 5!</span>

  <span id="freeText11708638064954761059" style="display:none">This is where the series really hits its stride. <div id="review_229955546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229955546" />
    <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez"><img alt="Anthony Chavez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314570438p2/4876333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229955546?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Chavez" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez">Anthony Chavez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12550348-the-sandman-vol-4">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876333-anthony-chavez?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876333-anthony-chavez?shelf=graphic-novel-manga">graphic-novel-manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229955546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8419353510926071525">What happens when Lucifer decides to leave hell? Season of Mists, the fourth volume of The Sandman answers that question as Dream heads to Hell once again, this time to release a former lover who has been imprisoned and tortured for thousands of years. Upon arrival, he finds Hell deserted, and Lucifer ushering out the stragglers he has banished from the lands, he then hands dream the key to the kingdom. <br/><br/>This is the best of the first four volumes in the series, with "A Doll's House" a close secon</span>
  <span id="freeText8419353510926071525" style="display:none">What happens when Lucifer decides to leave hell? Season of Mists, the fourth volume of The Sandman answers that question as Dream heads to Hell once again, this time to release a former lover who has been imprisoned and tortured for thousands of years. Upon arrival, he finds Hell deserted, and Lucifer ushering out the stragglers he has banished from the lands, he then hands dream the key to the kingdom. <br /><br />This is the best of the first four volumes in the series, with "A Doll's House" a close second, this should not be missed by fans, nor casual observers.<br /><br />Gaiman always adds epic storytelling and mythology in the series and this volume is no exception, Season of Mists takes on a lot: sin, redemption, both personal and religious, and the battle between good and evil. To discuss too much of the plot would ruin some of the rich suprises to come, but Gaiman's inventiveness is to the max here, with a gleefully funny and fascinating scene involving intrigue and lobbying by any number of demons, gods, and demigods, this provides an interesting look at the interactions between them (Thor getting ridiculously drunk and hitting on women during the banquet, for example). There is also a great ghost story set in a boys school that's not really like any haunted house tale you've ever read. But in the midst of his epic scope, Gaiman never neglects the smaller and more intimate touches, and scenes involving nothing more than an unlikely character commenting on a sunset or an unexpected birth revealing unexpected depths and complexities to Gaiman's creations. The character of Lucifer is excellent and intriguing as well, and God's reward to the two angels who oversaw Dreams decision? Well, that's up to the reader to decide. It's become apparent just a little ways into the volume that Gaiman has constructed something akin to a new cosmology and mythology here, and while it's wonderful to get lost in his worlds, it's the surprisingly human characters that keep us enthralled and reading volume after volume.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8419353510926071525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_631616107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/631616107" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/631616107?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631616107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2540307747993427433">The speech of Lucifer Morningstar on giving up his responsibilities in Hell would be good enough to justify the five stars review, but there is a lot more to like in this new book of the Sandman comic. Like the old fashioned chapter headings, teasers of events to come and plot twists to discover:<br/><br/>issue 21 : <i> In which a Family reunion occasions certain recriminations; assorted events are set in motion; and a relationship thought long done with proves to have much relevance today. </i><br/><br/>The prologue brin</span>
  <span id="freeText2540307747993427433" style="display:none">The speech of Lucifer Morningstar on giving up his responsibilities in Hell would be good enough to justify the five stars review, but there is a lot more to like in this new book of the Sandman comic. Like the old fashioned chapter headings, teasers of events to come and plot twists to discover:<br><br>issue 21 : <i> In which a Family reunion occasions certain recriminations; assorted events are set in motion; and a relationship thought long done with proves to have much relevance today. </i><br><br>The prologue brings together for the first time the Sandman's family, at the behest of the Fates (The Maid / Mother / Crone triumvirate we have already met):<br><b>Destiny </b> is the oldest of the Endless; he sees the fine traceries the galaxies make as they spiral through the void, he watches the intricate patterns living things make on their journey through time. Destiny smells of dust and the libraries of night. <br>He leaves no footprints. <br>He casts no shadow.<br><br><b> Desire </b> Never a possession, always the possessor, with skin as pale as smoke, and eyes tawny and sharp like yellow wine: Desire is everything you ever wanted. Whoever you are. Whatever you are. Everything.<br><br>It is said that scattered through <b> Despair's </b> domain are a multitude of tiny windows, hanging in the void. Each window looks out on a different scene, being, in our world, a mirror. Sometimes you will look into a mirror and feel the eyes of <b> Despair </b> upon you, feel her hook catch and snag on your heart.<br><br><b> Delirium </b> is the youngest of the Endless. She smells of sweat, sour wines, late nights, old leather. <br><br><b> Dream </b> is rake-thin, with skin the colour of falling snow. He acumulates names to himself like others make friends; but he permits himself few friends.<br><br>There is a tale that one day in every century <b> Death </b> takes on mortal flesh, better to comprehend what the lives she takes must feel like, to taste the bitter tang of mortality; that this is the price she must pay for being the divider of the living from all that has gone before, all that must come after.<br><br>The seventh Endless is lost, or playing truant, but that's a tale for another time. For now, Dream has to return to Hell and claim back, Nada, the mortal he sent there after she refused his love.<br><br>issue 22: <i> In which the Lord of Dreams makes preparations to visit the realms infernal; farewells are said; a toast is drunk; and in Hell the Adversary makes certain preparations of his own. </i><br><br>The Sandman says good bye to his friends, he knows he may not return from the place he was warned off in an earlier issue. He also makes preparations for his succession: a child born in the realm of dreams is offered as a possible solution. Hob Gadling, one of the few mortal friends of the Sandman makes a cameo appearance and a toast:<br><i> To absent friends, lost loves, old gods, and the season of mists; an may each and every one of us always give the devil his due. </i><br><br>My favorite panels in this issue are about The Library od Dreams, a place similar in a way to Jasper Fforde's Well of Lost Plots or to Carlos Ruiz Zafon's Cemetery of Forgotten Books. I hope I will see more of it in future issues.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423945i/844953.jpg" alt="Lucien" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>issue 23: <i> In which the Lord of Dreams returns to Hell, and his confrontation with the lord of that realm; in which a number of doors are closed for the last time; and of the strange disposition of a knife and key. </i><br><br>This is probably the best single issue in the series so far. It looks at the realm of hell as the shadow of Heaven, <i> or more precisely, perhaps, Heaven's dark reflection - like a landscape hanging inverted in the waters of a lake... </i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423945i/844954.jpg" alt="Lucifer" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'll quote his rant in full, because it is too good to miss or truncate:<br><br><i> And the mortals! I ask you - why? Why do they blame for all their little failings? They use my name as if I spend the entire day sitting on their shoulders, forcing them to commit acts they would otherwise find repulsive. "The Devil made me do it." I have never made one of them do anything. Never. They live their own tiny lives. I do not live their lives for them. And then they die, and they come here (having transgressed against what they believed to be right), and expect us to fulfill their desire for pain and retribution. I don't make them come here. They talk of me going around and buying souls, like a fishwife come to market day, never stopping to ask themselves why. I need no souls. No. They belong to themselves ...They just hate to have to face up to it. </i><br><br>Lucifer has had enough, he quits, empties Hell of all its inhabitants, locks out the realm and leaves Morpheus to sort out the mess.<br><br>I'll stop now with the chapter headings and with the detailed synopsis, after all, it would not do to spoil all the plot points. Suffice to say that Morpheus has a hot potato in his hands and must pass on the responsibilities for managing Hell before the demons and the dead returning to life invade the other realms. He will host a banquet in the Dreaming for all the parties interested - mythical creatures from all ages and cultures (Faerie, Valhalla, Egypt, the Roman Empire, angels, demons, oriental heroes, chaos and order avatars). He will be offered bribes and blackmail and he will have to fight to impose his will on this unruly crowd. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423945i/844955.jpg" alt="myths" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Great stuff with a dose of black humor to temper the horror parts, capital writing, decent graphics that may be sometimes a letdown for me, but are easy to ignore as I follow the story.<br><br>Onward to book five.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2540307747993427433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=90-s-horror">90-s-horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627828880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15378298291364904015">This is my favorite entry in the Sandman series so far!<br/><br/>Here we learn a lot-for instance, all the supposed stand alone stories in Sandman 3: The Dream Country, were NOT all stand alones. Some of them do have connections that are referenced here. <br/><br/>The introduction by the irascible Harlan Ellison was fantastic. I know he's a curmudgeon, but I adore the man. His description of what happened when one of Gaiman's comic book stories won the World Fantasy Award was freaking hilarious. <br/><br/>I didn't enjoy the </span>
  <span id="freeText15378298291364904015" style="display:none">This is my favorite entry in the Sandman series so far!<br /><br />Here we learn a lot-for instance, all the supposed stand alone stories in Sandman 3: The Dream Country, were NOT all stand alones. Some of them do have connections that are referenced here. <br /><br />The introduction by the irascible Harlan Ellison was fantastic. I know he's a curmudgeon, but I adore the man. His description of what happened when one of Gaiman's comic book stories won the World Fantasy Award was freaking hilarious. <br /><br />I didn't enjoy the artwork in this one as much as I did in previous volumes, but I loved and admired the stories and the writing so much, that I didn't mind. I would have enjoyed these stories with no artwork at all. <br /><br />It is now becoming clear to me what an epic undertaking this series must have been. The story arc is HUGE and encompasses so much. We have hell and demons and all kinds of creatures from legends and myths and they're all mashed together in a story that somehow makes sense. It's truly impressive and I can't wait to continue on with this series.<br /><br />Highly recommended to fans of fantasy, Neil Gaiman and graphic novels. </span>

<div id="review_3110926843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3110926843" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3110926843?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110926843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer667054989505840155">This 4th volume in the series starts with the Endless gathering. We learn there is one who left their company, a brother they all miss. But that is neither here nor there (at first). Destiny, who initiated the meeting after the Fates talked to him, doesn't tell them what it's about until it has happened. Death (my favourite) teaches her brother Morpheus a thing or two about manners and pride - a long overdue lesson if you ask me - and thus the Dream Lord finally realizes what fool he's been abou</span>
  <span id="freeText667054989505840155" style="display:none">This 4th volume in the series starts with the Endless gathering. We learn there is one who left their company, a brother they all miss. But that is neither here nor there (at first). Destiny, who initiated the meeting after the Fates talked to him, doesn't tell them what it's about until it has happened. Death (my favourite) teaches her brother Morpheus a thing or two about manners and pride - a long overdue lesson if you ask me - and thus the Dream Lord finally realizes what fool he's been about Nada and embarks on FINALLY setting her free!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233191._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But you guessed it: it means going back to Hell! Which means he has to encounter Lucifer Morningstar again, which could end with Morpheus actually losing, considering how they parted ways last time!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233190._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>However, the meeting goes completely different from what one might have expected and we get some of the best introspection on humanity and the hell myth. I always loved this notion because, personally, I think it's all a cop-out (what with the devil and sin and so on). Turns out, the Lightbringer agrees.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233192._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There were a few other gems that made me love this fallen angel.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233194._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Basically, this volume is all about Hell and what it means for the individual, the purpose it serves. It also deals with what would happen if Hell no longer existed (giving us some of the seeds that turned into the spin-off with the Morningstar).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233193._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>One more picture because I love this quote so much:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586032069i/29233195._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Once again, the art is nothing too pretty though it has its moments. However, the story was PERFECT! Seriously, this has become my instant favourite (so far). All the deities and creatures assembled, all the mythologies we touch upon (mostly correctly represented too), the essential questions posed ... this volume was sooo rich with thought-provoking (dream) stuff and I loved every second of it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="667054989505840155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290474369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1166486068462933990">I'm starting to think maybe these comics just aren't for me. This was hard to get through. I enjoyed the first scene where Dream and his siblings get together. Most of the story involved Dream going to Hell to retrieve a woman he had condemned there 10,000 years ago for rejecting him (what a dick). Lucifer doesn't even want to be King of Hell anymore and gives it to Dream. He doesn't want it either and ends up giving it back to two angels. So Hell will be Hell once again, but with angels oversee</span>
  <span id="freeText1166486068462933990" style="display:none">I'm starting to think maybe these comics just aren't for me. This was hard to get through. I enjoyed the first scene where Dream and his siblings get together. Most of the story involved Dream going to Hell to retrieve a woman he had condemned there 10,000 years ago for rejecting him (what a dick). Lucifer doesn't even want to be King of Hell anymore and gives it to Dream. He doesn't want it either and ends up giving it back to two angels. So Hell will be Hell once again, but with angels overseeing things. They still gotta make sure all the torturing and suffering and gnashing of teeth continues. It is hell, after all.<br /><br />I kind of feel like when I read American Gods and Stardust. It's was good, but kind of meh. It just goes on and on, the writing. And yeah, sometimes it seems a bit pretentious. I'll probably keep reading, but I have to take breaks between these. They aren't binge-read material, in my view.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1166486068462933990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44824883-paul-e-morph?shelf=comics-read-in-2020">comics-read-in-2020</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5787396894879784145">Writing’s still amazing. Artwork’s still a bit ropey in places, although Dringenberg’s stuff is getting a lot better.<br/><br/>What more do you want from me? Read it yourself.</span>

<div id="review_300899284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300899284" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300899284?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Sandman Fans!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=neil-gaiman">neil-gaiman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=vertigo-comics">vertigo-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300899284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1522754347598533631">After reading more of Neil Gaiman’s classic “Sandman” series, I never would have thought that the stories would get better and better and the fourth volume “Season of Mists” certainly did not disappoint me! Dream (Morpheus) definitely got his hands full in this volume that will reveal many shocking surprises for the fans of the fantastic “Sandman” series!<br/><br/>In this volume “Season of Mists,” when a family meeting between the Endless ends up revealing Dream’s past horrible deed of condemning the woma</span>
  <span id="freeText1522754347598533631" style="display:none">After reading more of Neil Gaiman’s classic “Sandman” series, I never would have thought that the stories would get better and better and the fourth volume “Season of Mists” certainly did not disappoint me! Dream (Morpheus) definitely got his hands full in this volume that will reveal many shocking surprises for the fans of the fantastic “Sandman” series!<br /><br />In this volume “Season of Mists,” when a family meeting between the Endless ends up revealing Dream’s past horrible deed of condemning the woman he loved, Nada, to the Underworld, Dream decides to go down to the Underworld to rescue Nada. Unfortunately, Lucifer Morningstar, who vowed to destroy Dream after Dream humiliated him in the first volume, has plans for Dream that might end up turning Dream’s world into a nightmare! Instead of having separate stories in this volume, this volume is broken up in chapters and it has a total of six chapters along with a prologue and an epilogue.<br /><br />Neil Gaiman has once again created a story from the popular “Sandman” series that will continue to stand the test of time to many generations! The fourth volume of Neil Gaiman’s “Sandman” series is just as enjoyable as the first two volumes as it details Dream’s efforts to rescue his former lover Nada from the depths of the Underworld. I loved the way that Neil Gaiman made the atmosphere of this story extremely dark yet adventurous at the same time as the majority of this volume takes place in the Underworld and I was so shocked at seeing the horrible activities that takes place in the Underworld. I also loved the religious references that Neil Gaiman brings to this volume as there are many references about the balance between Heaven and Hell and I loved how it was explained through this story. The character Lucifer Morningstar proved to be an interesting antagonist in this volume as Neil Gaiman did a brilliant job of laying out his plot against Dream step by step and the burden that he placed on Dream was cleverly plotted and as I keep on reading more about Lucifer’s plan throughout this volume, I wanted to know how Dream was going to beat Lucifer at his own game. Kelley Jones, Mike Dringenberg, Malcolm Jones III, Matt Wagner, Dick Giordano, George Pratt and P. Craig Russell’s artwork were brilliant in this volume as they each brought their own unique flair to the story. I loved the illustrations of the Underworld that each artist brought because the images of the Underworld were brilliant and disturbing at the same time and it really brought out the intensity in this story.<br /><br />Like the first three volumes of the “Sandman” series, there is some disturbing content in this volume, especially with the scenes of the Underworld. In the Underworld sequences, there are many images of people being tortured such as an image of a man who has nails embedded in his body and chains that pulled at his skin and some images of people being impaled by sharp staffs. Also, there are some images of nudity in this volume that might offend some people who do not like seeing nudity in images. <br /><br />Overall, “The Sandman: Season of Mists” is a truly brilliant and haunting volume for fans of Neil Gaiman’s “Sandman” series and will surely be a pure delight to read for many years. I would recommend this volume to readers ages sixteen and up since there are many disturbing images and some nudity that some people might not enjoy reading. Now I am off to read the fifth volume in the “Sandman” series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25102.The_Sandman__Vol__5_A_Game_of_You" title="The Sandman, Vol. 5 A Game of You by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sandman, Vol. 5: A Game of You</a>.<br /><br /><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/03/sandman-season-of-mists-volume-4-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1522754347598533631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_309315799" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309315799" />
    <a title="Nicolo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/533046-nicolo"><img alt="Nicolo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320768283p2/533046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309315799?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicolo" href="/user/show/533046-nicolo">Nicolo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781563890413" href="/book/show/104596.Season_of_Mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/533046-nicolo?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309315799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16754900329004452540">Beware of gifts from the Devil, a lesson that Dream learned too late when he entered the realm of Hell, ready to do battle with Lucifer if necessary, only to have the Lord of Hell tell his gift he was closing shop. There was to be no battle unless Dream wanted it so and only a gift for his guest, the key of Hell. Now the reluctant owner of a prime piece of psychic real estate, Morpheus gets embroiled by a series of supplicants from various pantheons seeking the key and eager to offer gifts, thre</span>
  <span id="freeText16754900329004452540" style="display:none">Beware of gifts from the Devil, a lesson that Dream learned too late when he entered the realm of Hell, ready to do battle with Lucifer if necessary, only to have the Lord of Hell tell his gift he was closing shop. There was to be no battle unless Dream wanted it so and only a gift for his guest, the key of Hell. Now the reluctant owner of a prime piece of psychic real estate, Morpheus gets embroiled by a series of supplicants from various pantheons seeking the key and eager to offer gifts, threats and bribes for it.<br /><br />This was Lucifer’s perfect revenge for a slight he received from Morpheus in the opening arc. In abdicating Hell he changed his destiny, no longer was he the warden for souls seeking torment and punishment for their sins. Lucifer was free and now Morpheus was vexed, not knowing what to do with the key.<br /><br />The themes of change and freedom that occur when a king gives up his kingdom are a familiar refrain that would be revisited in later volumes in Neil Gaiman’s <i>Sandman</i>. Gaiman is one of earliest writers who’ve used the comic book medium to craft stories that make you think, others of this ilk are his fellow Brits and they helped usher comic books from adolescent escapist pamphlets to mature stories that helped the medium gain acceptance as a legitimate art form.<br /> <br />In this volume, much of Gaiman story in volume is enhanced by the talents of his art team. The meat of the story is penciled by Kelley Jones, whose visceral style gives us a Hell that would bring one nightmares. A framing sequence is provided by Mike Dringenbery in what would be his coda to the series. He is credited for defining the look of the Endless, especially of Death, in whom he receives a co-creating credit. This would be the last time his understated and realistic style would grace this title.<br /><br />This is one of the more memorable <i>Sandman</i> stories, it introduces Hell, the existence of various pantheons and a woman who had spurned Dream. A lot characters that made their debut here would prove to be important in succeeding stories as they assume larger roles in the saga of Morpheus. It is an excellent story and it opens up a lot of possibilities for the character,<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16754900329004452540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
